class="!text-title-h5 [&amp;:not(:first-child)]:mt-72 mb-24 relative"><span class="absolute -top-[120px]" id="introduction"></span><h2 class="!text-title-h5">Introduction</h2></div>
<p>Last week marked an exciting milestone for Firecrawl as we kicked off our inaugural Launch Week, unveiling a series of new features and updates designed to enhance your web scraping experience. Let&#x27;s take a look back at the improvements we introduced throughout the week.</p>
<div class="!text-title-h5 [&amp;:not(:first-child)]:mt-72 mb-24 relative"><span class="absolute -top-[120px]" id="[object-object]"></span><h2 class="!text-title-h5"><a class="!underline" href="https://firecrawl.dev/blog/launch-week-i-day-1-introducing-teams">Day 1: Introducing Teams</a></h2></div>
<p>We started Launch Week by introducing our highly anticipated Teams feature. Teams enables seamless collaboration on web scraping projects, allowing you to work alongside your colleagues and tackle complex data gathering tasks together. With updated pricing plans to accommodate teams of all sizes, Firecrawl is now an excellent platform for collaborative web scraping.</p>
<div class="!text-title-h5 [&amp;:not(:first-child)]:mt-72 mb-24 relative"><span class="absolute -top-[120px]" id="[object-object]"></span><h2 class="!text-title-h5"><a class="!underline" href="https://firecrawl.dev/blog/launch-week-i-day-2-doubled-rate-limits">Day 2: Increased Rate Limits</a></h2></div>
<p>On Day 2, we improved your data collection capabilities by doubling the rate limits for our /scrape endpoint across all plans. This means you can now gather more data in the same amount of time, enabling you to take on larger projects and scrape more frequently.</p>
<div class="!text-title-h5 [&amp;:not(:first-child)]:mt-72 mb-24 relative"><span class="absolute -top-[120px]" id="[object-object]"></span><h2 class="!text-title-h5"><a class="!underline" href="https://firecrawl.dev/blog/launch-week-i-day-3-introducing-map-endpoint">Day 3: Introducing the Map Endpoint (Alpha)</a></h2></div>
<p>Day 3 saw the unveiling of our new Map endpoint, which allows you to transform a single URL into a comprehensive map of an entire website quickly. As a fast and easy way to gather all the URLs on a website, the Map endpoint opens up new possibilities for your web scraping projects.</p>
<div class="!text-title-h5 [&amp;:not(:first-child)]:mt-72 mb-24 relative"><span class="absolute -top-[120px]" id="[object-object]"></span><h2 class="!text-title-h5"><a class="!underline" href="https://firecrawl.dev/blog/launch-week-i-day-4-introducing-firecrawl-v1">Day 4: Introducing Firecrawl /v1</a></h2></div>
<p>Day 4 marked a significant release: Firecrawl /v1. This more reliable and developer-friendly API makes gathering web data easier. With new scrape formats, improved crawl status, enhanced markdown parsing, v1 support for all SDKs (including new Go and Rust SDKs), and an improved developer experience, v1 enhances your web scraping workflow.</p>
<div class="!text-title-h5 [&amp;:not(:first-child)]:mt-72 mb-24 relative"><span class="absolute -top-[120px]" id="[object-object]"></span><h2 class="!text-title-h5"><a class="!underline" href="https://firecrawl.dev/blog/launch-week-i-day-5-real-time-crawling-websockets">Day 5: Real-Time Crawling with WebSockets</a></h2></div>
<p>On Day 5, we introduced a new feature: Real-Time Crawling with WebSockets. Our WebSocket-based method, Crawl URL and Watch, enables real-time data extraction and monitoring, allowing you to process data immediately, react to errors quickly, and know precisely when your crawl is complete.</p>
<div class="!text-title-h5 [&amp;:not(:first-child)]:mt-72 mb-24 relative"><span class="absolute -top-[120px]" id="[object-object]"></span><h2 class="!text-title-h5"><a class="!underline" href="https://firecrawl.dev/blog/launch-week-i-day-6-llm-extract">Day 6: LLM Extract (v1)</a></h2></div>
<p>Day 6 brought v1 support for LLM Extract, enabling you to extract structured data from web pages using the extract format in /scrape. With the ability to pass a schema or just provide a prompt, LLM extraction is now more flexible and powerful.</p>
<div class="!text-title-h5 [&amp;:not(:first-child)]:mt-72 mb-24 relative"><span class="absolute -top-[120px]" id="[object-object]"></span><h2 class="!text-title-h5"><a class="!underline" href="https://firecrawl.dev/blog/launch-week-i-day-7-webhooks">Day 7: Crawl Webhooks (v1)</a></h2></div>
<p>We wrapped up Launch Week with the introduction of /crawl webhook support. You can now send notifications to your apps during a crawl, with four types of events: crawl.started, crawl.page, crawl.completed, and crawl.failed. This feature allows for more seamless integration of Firecrawl into your workflows.</p>
<div class="!text-title-h5 [&amp;:not(:first-child)]:mt-72 mb-24 relative"><span class="absolute -top-[120px]" id="wrapping-up"></span><h2 class="!text-title-h5">Wrapping Up</h2></div>
<p>Launch Week showcased our commitment to continually evolving and improving Firecrawl to meet the needs of our users. From collaborative features like Teams to performance improvements like increased rate limits, and from new endpoints like Map and Extract to real-time capabilities with WebSockets and Webhooks, we&#x27;ve expanded the possibilities for your web scraping projects.</p>
<p>We&#x27;d like to thank our community for your support, feedback, and enthusiasm throughout Launch Week and beyond. Your input drives us to innovate and push the boundaries of what&#x27;s possible with web scraping.</p>
<p>Stay tuned for more updates as we continue to shape the future of data gathering together. Happy scraping!</p></div></div></div><div class="h-42 p-30 border-t border-border-faint relative lg-max:hidden"><svg fill="none" height="21" viewBox="0 0 11 21" width="11" misunderstand websites because they lack structured context. The llms.txt standard fixes this by providing a clear, machine-readable overview of your site—like a sitemap for AI. The **llms.txt Generator**, powered by Firecrawl, automates the entire process, turning your website into structured files that LLMs can accurately understand.\n\n## TL;DR\n\n- **What it is**: A tool that creates llms.txt files—standardized markdown documents that help AI understand your website\n- **How it works**: Firecrawl crawls your site and formats content into LLM-friendly files using gpt-4o-mini\n- **Access**: Use the web interface at [llmstxt.firecrawl.dev](https://llmstxt.firecrawl.dev/) or call the API directly\n- **Cost**: Free to use; optional Firecrawl API key removes limits\n- **Why it matters**: Improves how AI assistants, chatbots, and coding tools interact with your content\n\n## What is an llms.txt file?\n\nAn `llms.txt` file is a standardized markdown file proposed by Jeremy Howard to provide information to help LLMs use a website at inference time.\n\n\u003cdiv style={{ maxWidth: 550, margin: \"0 auto\" }}\u003e\n  \u003ciframe\n    src=\"https://platform.twitter.com/embed/Tweet.html?id=1831089138571133290\u0026lang=en\u0026theme=light\u0026dnt=true\"\n    style={{ width: \"100%\", height: \"clamp(420px, 70vh, 900px)\", border: 0 }}\n    loading=\"lazy\"\n    title=\"Embedded Tweet\"\n  /\u003e\n\u003c/div\u003e\n\nUnlike traditional web content designed for human readers, `llms.txt` files offer concise, structured information that LLMs can quickly ingest. This is particularly useful for enhancing development environments, providing documentation for programming libraries, and offering structured overviews for various domains such as corporate websites, educational institutions, and personal portfolios.\n\n**Use your data:** Once you've created your llms.txt file, use it in [RAG frameworks](/blog/best-open-source-rag-frameworks) for knowledge-augmented AI or with [MCP servers](/blog/best-mcp-servers-for-cursor) to enhance your development environment.\n\nThe `llms.txt` file is located at the root path `/llms.txt` of a website and contains sections in a specific order, including a project name, a summary, detailed information, and file lists with URLs for further details. This format allows LLMs to efficiently access and process the most important information about a website.\n\n### Why your website needs an llms.txt file\n\nMaking your content accessible to AI tools is becoming as important as traditional SEO. Here's why adding an llms.txt file matters:\n\n| Benefit                              | Description                                                                                                   |\n| ------------------------------------ | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |\n| **Improved AI discoverability**      | LLMs can find and understand your content more accurately, similar to how search engines use sitemaps         |\n| **Better context for AI assistants** | Coding assistants and chatbots get structured documentation instead of guessing from scattered pages          |\n| **Reduced hallucinations**           | Providing clean, organized content helps AI models give more accurate responses about your product or service |\n| **Developer-friendly documentation** | Technical content becomes instantly usable in AI-powered development tools and workflows                      |\n| **Future-proof your content**        | As AI agents become more common, standardized formats ensure your site remains accessible to new tools        |\n\n## Introducing llms.txt Generator ✨\n\nThe llms.txt Generator leverages [Firecrawl](https://www.firecrawl.dev) to crawl your website and extracts data using **gpt-4o-mini**. You can generate both `llms.txt` and `llms-full.txt` files through the web interface or via API.\n\n## Accessing llms.txt via API\n\nYou can access `llms.txt` directly by making a GET request to:\n\n```\nhttp://llmstxt.firecrawl.dev/{YOUR_URL}\n```\n\nFor the full version, use:\n\n```\nhttp://llmstxt.firecrawl.dev/{YOUR_URL}/full\n```\n\nIf you have a Firecrawl API key, you can include it to unlock full results and remove limits:\n\n```\nhttp://llmstxt.firecrawl.dev/{YOUR_URL}?FIRECRAWL_API_KEY=YOUR_API_KEY\n```\n\nFor the full version with API key:\n\n```\nhttp://llmstxt.firecrawl.dev/{YOUR_URL}/full?FIRECRAWL_API_KEY=YOUR_API_KEY\n```\n\n## How to generate your llms.txt file\n\n1. **Visit the generator**: Go to [http://llmstxt.firecrawl.dev](http://llmstxt.firecrawl.dev).\n\n2. **Enter your website URL**: Input the URL of your website.\n\n3. **Generate the file**: Click the generate button and wait a few minutes as the tool processes your site.\n\n4. **Download your files**: Once ready, download the `llms.txt` and `llms-full.txt` files.\n\n## No API key required, but recommended\n\nWhile an API key is not required, using a free Firecrawl API key removes any usage limits and provides full access to all features.\n\n## Good to know: llms.txt vs robots.txt and sitemap.xml\n\nThese three files serve different purposes in making your website accessible, but they often work together. Here's what you need to know:\n\n| File            | Primary Purpose                | Target Audience                 | Content Format                            |\n| --------------- | ------------------------------ | ------------------------------- | ----------------------------------------- |\n| **robots.txt**  | Controls what bots can crawl   | Search engines and web crawlers | Simple directives (allow/disallow)        |\n| **sitemap.xml** | Lists all pages for indexing   | Search engines                  | Structured XML with URLs and metadata     |\n| **llms.txt**    | Provides context and summaries | Large Language Models           | Human-readable markdown with descriptions |\n\n**Key differences to remember:**\n\n- **robots.txt** restricts access; llms.txt and sitemap.xml provide access\n- **sitemap.xml** lists every page; llms.txt summarizes key content and structure\n- **llms.txt** includes natural language descriptions that LLMs can understand, not just URLs\n- You need all three files for complete site discoverability: robots.txt for access control, sitemap.xml for traditional search, llms.txt for AI tools\n- Unlike robots.txt (which bots may ignore), llms.txt is a voluntary standard that AI tools choose to use\n\n## Why llms.txt is still important in 2026\n\nWhen the llms.txt standard first emerged, some dismissed it as another passing trend. Two years later, it's clear that was wrong. Here's why llms.txt matters more than ever:\n\n**AI agents are everywhere now.** What started as chatbots has evolved into autonomous agents that browse, research, and take action across the web. These agents need structured context to work effectively—and llms.txt provides exactly that. Without it, agents waste tokens parsing irrelevant content or, worse, misunderstand your site entirely.\n\n**Context windows got bigger, but so did the web.** Yes, models can now handle massive inputs. But that doesn't mean they should ingest your entire site. llms.txt gives AI the signal of what actually matters, cutting through noise to deliver the content that defines who you are and what you do.\n\n**The RAG ecosystem exploded.** Retrieval-augmented generation is now the default architecture for knowledge-intensive applications. llms.txt files slot perfectly into RAG pipelines—they're pre-structured, information-dense, and designed for exactly this use case. If your content isn't in llms.txt format, you're making it harder for developers to build on top of your data.\n\n**AI-first discovery is real.** People aren't just Googling anymore. They're asking Claude, ChatGPT, and Perplexity. If your site doesn't have structured content that LLMs can understand, you're invisible to a growing segment of how people find information. Think of llms.txt as SEO for the AI era.\n\n**Standards won.** The llms.txt format gained adoption because it's simple, human-readable, and solves a real problem. Major documentation sites, SaaS products, and developer tools now ship with llms.txt files. If you're not on board, you're behind.\n\nThe bottom line: llms.txt isn't a nice-to-have anymore. It's infrastructure for the AI-native web.\n\n## Related resources\n\n- Explore [web scraping libraries](/blog/best-open-source-web-scraping-libraries) for collecting website data\n- Learn about [browser automation tools](/blog/browser-automation-tools-comparison) for dynamic content extraction\n- Automate data collection with [n8n workflows](/blog/firecrawl-n8n-web-automation)\n- Build AI agents using your data with our [agent frameworks guide](/blog/best-open-source-agent-frameworks-2025)\n\n## Frequently asked questions\n\n**Q: Do I need to update my llms.txt file regularly?**\n\nA: Yes, update it when you add major content sections, change site structure, or launch new features. For dynamic sites, consider regenerating monthly or after significant updates.\n\n**Q: Can I manually edit the generated llms.txt file?**\n\nA: Absolutely. The generator creates a starting point, but you can edit the file to emphasize important sections, remove irrelevant content, or improve descriptions for better AI understanding.\n\n**Q: Will having an llms.txt file affect my search engine rankings?**\n\nA: No direct impact on traditional SEO. It's slow, expensive, and breaks constantly.\n\nYou need a better way to gather data at scale.\n\n## How /agent works\n\nDescribe what data you want to extract and /agent handles the rest.\n\n```python\nfrom firecrawl import FirecrawlApp\nfrom pydantic import BaseModel, Field\nfrom typing import List, Optional\n\napp = FirecrawlApp(api_key=\"fc-YOUR_API_KEY\")\n\nclass Company(BaseModel):\n    name: str = Field(description=\"Company name\")\n    contact_email: Optional[str] = Field(None, description=\"Contact email\")\n    employee_count: Optional[str] = Field(None, description=\"Number of employees\")\n\nclass CompaniesSchema(BaseModel):\n    companies: List[Company] = Field(description=\"List of companies\")\n\nresult = app.agent(\n    prompt=\"Find YC W24 dev tool companies and get their contact info and team size\",\n    schema=CompaniesSchema\n)\n\nprint(result.data)\n```\n\nNo URLs required. Your documentation is great, your website is packed with information, but users still ask the same questions over and over. \n\nYou know the solution: a smart, AI-powered chatbot that can answer questions based on your content.\n\nBut building a production-grade retrieval-augmented generation (RAG) pipeline is a massive undertaking. It involves scraping, cleaning, chunking, embedding, storing, retrieving, and generating. Third-party services can help, but they often come with limitations (like locking you into their ecosystem).\n\nSo, we asked ourselves: **What if you could create a production-ready RAG pipeline and a ready-to-use chatbot for any website in under 60 seconds?**\n\nThis is the story of Firestarter.\n\n## **Enter a URL. Get a chatbot.**\n\nFirestarter is a complete Next.js chatbot-building platform that we've made as simple as possible. It's a new addition to our [open-source AI toolbox](https://www.firecrawl.dev/blog/fire-enrich), designed to make chatbot creation accessible to everyone:\n\n1. Enter any website URL (e.g., [https://docs.firecrawl.dev](https://docs.firecrawl.dev))\n2. **Click \"Start\"** and watch as it crawls and indexes the content in real-time\n3. **Instantly get** a full-featured chat interface and a developer-ready, OpenAI-compatible API\n\nBehind this simple UI is a sophisticated, pre-built RAG pipeline that handles the entire workflow from raw website to intelligent, queryable data source, powered by Firecrawl for web scraping and Upstash for serverless vector search.\n\nThe system is architected to let you build and deploy multiple chatbots based on as many websites as you'd like—each one completely independent with its own data namespace and API endpoint.\n\n## **How it works: From website to wisdom**\n\nFirestarter isn't just a simple script; it's a complete, two-phase system for creating and interacting with knowledge bases.\n\n### **Phase 1: The indexing engine**\n\nWhen you enter a URL, Firestarter kicks off a meticulous process:\n\n1. **Smart Crawling**: It uses Firecrawl to navigate the site, fetching the clean, structured Markdown content of each page. This bypasses the need to deal with raw HTML, ads, and other noise.\\\n   \\\\\n2. **Intelligent Indexing**: The content is streamed directly to an [Upstash search index](https://upstash.com/docs/search/overall/getstarted). Upstash automatically chunks the text, creates vector embeddings, and stores them in a high-performance, serverless vector database.\\\n   \\\\\n3. **Namespace Creation**: The entire crawl is isolated under a unique namespace (e.g., firecrawl-dev-1718394041), ensuring each chatbot's data is separate and secure.\\\n   \\\\\n\n### **Phase 2: The RAG-Powered Brain**\n\nOnce indexed, your chatbot is live. When a user asks a question:\n\n1. **[Semantic Search](https://www.firecrawl.dev/blog/best-semantic-search-apis)**: Firestarter queries the Upstash index, searching for the most relevant document chunks based on the _meaning_ of the question, not just keywords.\\\n   \\\\\n2. **Context-Aware Prompting**: The most relevant chunks are compiled into a context block. This, along with the original question, is sent to your choice of LLM—OpenAI, Anthropic, Groq, or any LLM you like. Built with the Vercel AI SDK, there's full flexibility to customize and use any LLM provider you decide to use.\\\n   \\\\\n3. **Streaming Response**: The LLM generates the answer, which is streamed back to the UI in real-time using the Vercel AI SDK, providing a smooth, human-like chat experience.\\\n   \\\\\n\n**The best part?** Every step is transparent. \n\nAnd for developers, Firestarter creates something truly special: an **OpenAI-compatible API endpoint** for every single chatbot. \n\nThis means you can use the official OpenAI libraries in any language to programmatically query your website's content, treating it like a structured, intelligent database.\n\n## **This is just the beginning**\n\nProduction-grade RAG is complex. Our goal with Firestarter isn't to be a closed, perfect-out-of-the-box solution.\n\nInstead, we want to build a powerful, open source foundation that anyone can use, understand, and contribute to.\n\nThe version you see in this repository is our first major step. It works, it provides immense value, but we know there's room to grow. For most web tasks, that's enough.\n\nBut when it comes to pagination, form fills, and auth flows, agents need an integrated browser to navigate and extract hard-to-reach data. A static scrape won't get you through a login page. Search won't click through a multi-step pricing flow. And local browser tooling means CPU spikes, Chromium installs, and infrastructure you have to maintain.\n\nThis is why we're launching Firecrawl Browser Sandbox.\n\n## What is Browser Sandbox?\n\nBrowser Sandbox is a secure, remote browser environment your agents can control. Each session runs in an isolated container - fully managed by Firecrawl, with nothing running on your local machine.\n\nEvery sandbox comes pre-loaded with the tools agents already use:\n\n- **Playwright** - for precise browser control and scripting\n- **Agent Browser** - for autonomous, AI-driven navigation\n\nNo setup. No configuration. Call it from the CLI or API and your agent has a browser ready in seconds. [Read the docs →](https://docs.firecrawl.dev/features/browser)\n\n## How it works\n\n```bash\n# Install CLI, auth, and add skills to all your agents\nnpx -y firecrawl-cli@latest init --all --browser\n\n# Install Browser Sandbox via CLI\nnpm install -g firecrawl-cli\n\n# Use Browser Sandbox\nfirecrawl browser \"open uspto.gov\"\n```\n\n```python\nfrom firecrawl import Firecrawl\n\napp = Firecrawl(api_key=\"fc-YOUR-API-KEY\")\n\nresponse = app.list_browsers()\nprint(response.sessions)\n```\n\n## Key capabilities\n\n### Fully managed sandbox, secure and scalable\n\nEvery session runs in an isolated, disposable environment. Agents and the sites they visit are fully contained within the sandbox, so you can run code securely without risk to your own infrastructure.\n\nSince nothing runs locally, there are no CPU or RAM spikes on your machine. And you can launch parallel sessions - each in its own sandbox - scaling from one browser to hundreds without managing anything.\n\n### Zero config, pre-loaded with the tools agents already use\n\nBrowser Sandbox comes pre-loaded with Playwright and Agent Browser, so your agents have everything they need to interact with the web. No Chromium to install, no browser framework to configure.\n\nCompatible with Claude Code, Codex, OpenCode, and more.\n\n### Persistent or temporary sessions - you choose\n\nPersistent sessions let you create profiles where auth and state carry across runs. Your agents can pick up where they left off - no re-logging in, no re-navigating. Ideal for workflows that span multiple sessions or require saved credentials.\n\nTemporary sessions are the opposite: clean, disposable browsers that spin up fresh every time. Perfect for one-off extracts where you don't need any state to carry over.\n\n### Fully interactive\n\nBrowser sessions are fully interactive. You can click around alongside your agents, watching what they do and stepping in when you need to.\n\n### Scrape, search, and browse - all through Firecrawl\n\nBrowser Sandbox works alongside Firecrawl's existing scrape and search endpoints. Instead of stitching together separate tools, agents can navigate pagination, fill out forms, and work through multi-step flows to get data that scraping alone can't reach - all through a single platform.\n\nWhen to use Browser and other Firecrawl endpoints:\n\n| Use Case | Right Tool |\n| --- | --- |\n| Extract content from a known URL | Scrape |\n| Search the web and get results | Search |\n| Navigate pagination, fill forms, click through flows | Browser |\n| Multi-step workflows with interaction | Browser |\n| Parallel browsing across many sites | Browser (each session is isolated) |\n\nHere's Firecrawl Browser Sandbox fetching dozens of patents with a single prompt:\n\n![Firecrawl Browser Sandbox fetching patents](/images/blog/browser-sandbox-launch/browser-sandbox-example.gif)\n\n## Real-world use cases\n\n**Competitive intelligence**\n\nYour agent browses competitor sites, navigates search forms and filters, and extracts pricing, features, and positioning into structured data. When you are shipping fast, data is bound to get stale, with Firecrawl and LLMs you can make sure your public web data is always consistent! We will be using Opus's huge 200k context window and Firecrawl's parellization, making this process accurate and fast.\n\n## Setup\n\nInstall our python dependencies, including anthropic and firecrawl-py.\n\n```bash\npip install firecrawl-py anthropic\n```\n\n## Getting your Claude and Firecrawl API Keys\n\nTo use Claude Opus and Firecrawl, you will need to get your API keys. You can get your Anthropic API key from [here](https://www.anthropic.com/) and your Firecrawl API key from [here](https://firecrawl.dev).\n\n## Load website with Firecrawl\n\nTo be able to get all the data from our website page put it into an easy to read format for the LLM, we will use [Firecrawl](https://firecrawl.dev). It handles by-passing JS-blocked websites, extracting the main content, and outputting in a LLM-readable format for increased accuracy.\n\nHere is how we will scrape a website url using Firecrawl-py\n\n```python\nfrom firecrawl import FirecrawlApp\n\napp = FirecrawlApp(api_key=\"YOUR-KEY\")\n\ncrawl_result = app.crawl_url('mendable.ai', {'crawlerOptions': {'excludes': ['blog/.+','usecases/.+']}})\n\nprint(crawl_result)\n```\n\nWith all of the web data we want scraped and in a clean format, we can move onto the next step.\n\n## Combination and Generation\n\nNow that we have the website data, let's pair up every page and run every combination through Opus for analysis.\n\n```python\nfrom itertools import combinations\n\npage_combinations = []\n\nfor first_page, second_page in combinations(crawl_result, 2):\n    combined_string = \"First Page:\\n\" + first_page['markdown'] + \"\\n\\nSecond Page:\\n\" + second_page['markdown']\n    page_combinations.append(combined_string)\n\nimport anthropic\n\nclient = anthropic.Anthropic(\n    # defaults to os.environ.get(\"ANTHROPIC_API_KEY\")\n    api_key=\"YOUR-KEY\",\n)\n\nfinal_output = []\n\nfor page_combination in page_combinations:\n\n    prompt = \"Here are two pages from a companies website, your job is to find any contradictions or differences in opinion between the two pages, this could be caused by outdated information or other. If you find any contradictions, list them out and provide a brief explanation of why they are contradictory or differing. Make sure the explanation is specific and concise. It is okay if you don't find any contradictions, just say 'No contradictions found' and nothing else. Here are the pages: \" + \"\\n\\n\".join(page_combination)\n\n    message = client.messages.create(\n        model=\"claude-3-opus-20240229\",\n        max_tokens=1000,\n        temperature=0.0,\n        system=\"You are an assistant that helps find contradictions or differences in opinion between pages in a company website and knowledge base. This could be caused by outdated information in the knowledge base.\",\n        messages=[\n            {\"role\": \"user\", \"content\": prompt}\n        ]\n    )\n    final_output.append(message.content)\n\n```\n\n## That's about it!\n\nYou have now built an agent that looks at your website and spots any inconsistencies it might have.\n\nIf you have any questions or need help, feel free to reach out to us at [Firecrawl](https://firecrawl.dev).\n"])</script><script>self.__next_f.push([1,"a6:Ta19,"])</script><script>self.__next_f.push([1,"\n*Athena Intelligence uses Firecrawl to ingest web content into their AI-native analytics platform, giving enterprise analysts an AI coworker that can read and reason about the internet.*\n\n**What is Athena Intelligence?** Athena Intelligence is an AI-native analytics platform purpose-built for regulated industries, helping enterprises in finance, law, defense, audit, and consulting delegate complex research and operational workflows to Athena, their AI digital coworker.\n\nWhen you're building an AI analyst for Fortune 500 enterprises, the quality of its output depends on the breadth and freshness of its web knowledge.
